  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d8fd7de5-cf75-4d53-9283-5a422fda326f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer856925292521240646">From the author of the international and <i>New York Times</i> bestseller <i>Let the Right One In (Let Me In)</i> comes this stunning and terrifying book which begins when a man's six-year-old daughter vanishes.   <span id="freeText856925292521240646" style="display:none">From the author of the international and <i>New York Times</i> bestseller <i>Let the Right One In (Let Me In)</i> comes this stunning and terrifying book which begins when a man's six-year-old daughter vanishes. One ordinary winter afternoon on a snowy island, Anders and Cecilia take their six-year-old daughter Maja across the ice to visit the lighthouse in the middle of the frozen channel. While the couple explore the lighthouse, Maja disappears -- either into thin air or under thin ice -- leaving not even a footprint in the snow. Two years later, alone and more or less permanently drunk, Anders returns to the island to regroup. He slowly realises that people are not telling him all they know; even his own mother, it seems, is keeping secrets. What is happening in Domaro, and what power does the sea have over the town's inhabitants?</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1519983-library-nerds-and-wordists----what">Library nerds and wordists---
What subject tags would ypu give this book? 
The subjects currently listed are: alcoholic fathers, dysfunctional families, island people, psychological fiction....

It doesn&#39;t really capture the essence of the book at all.... dysfunctional families? Really? Alcoholic fathers, really?</a>
</div>

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/3524597-aischa"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1417386740i/3524597._UX100_CR0,14,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/3524597-aischa">Aischa</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    What about the sea? The ancient give-take symbiotic relationship? Oceans-- Animism?<br />Fiction--possession? <br />The Deep? <br /><br />Everything falls flat. There must be<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    What about the sea? The ancient give-take symbiotic relationship? Oceans-- Animism?<br />Fiction--possession? <br />The Deep? <br /><br />Everything falls flat. There must be a word for the sea as an entity and it's relationship to man? Its sort of an elder god, but not... it seems like its a universal mythology of the sea. <br />Can subject headings be spoilers? <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_549208231" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/549208231" />
    <a title="Gabriel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/101529-gabriel"><img alt="Gabriel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1180845769p2/101529.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/549208231?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabriel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabriel" href="/user/show/101529-gabriel">Gabriel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer549208231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10917050750452632153">Umm ... wow.<br/><br/>In many ways, this feels like a conclusion to a trilogy rather than a standalone book. A trilogy that folds back in on itself and maybe, that's where the true horror lies. No, you don't have to read his previous two books (The famous <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/943402.Let_the_Right_One_In' title='Let the Right One In by John Ajvide Lindqvist' rel='nofollow noopener'>Let the Right One In</a> and generally misunderstood <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4328472.Handling_the_Undead' title='Handling the Undead by John Ajvide Lindqvist' rel='nofollow noopener'>Handling The Undead</a>) to enjoy Harbor. In many ways,for people looking for a book to start with, this is the one that should be the first John Lindqvist. I only wish I read it sooner ... but, like so many o</span>
  <span id="freeText10917050750452632153" style="display:none">Umm ... wow.<br /><br />In many ways, this feels like a conclusion to a trilogy rather than a standalone book. A trilogy that folds back in on itself and maybe, that's where the true horror lies. No, you don't have to read his previous two books (The famous <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/943402.Let_the_Right_One_In" title="Let the Right One In by John Ajvide Lindqvist" rel="nofollow noopener">Let the Right One In</a> and generally misunderstood <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4328472.Handling_the_Undead" title="Handling the Undead by John Ajvide Lindqvist" rel="nofollow noopener">Handling The Undead</a>) to enjoy Harbor. In many ways,for people looking for a book to start with, this is the one that should be the first John Lindqvist. I only wish I read it sooner ... but, like so many of my books, it sat on my shelf patiently biding its time, knowing I wouldn't resist for too long. <br /><br />I don't normally summarize in these reviews. I figure, you're all avid readers out there, you can read the book on your own (and there's a summary above), but this is one of those books that begs the question, "What is the real story?"<br /><br />So at first, we glimpse a normal family. Normal in that we have a child who is misbehaving, and two adults who love each other despite the strain the child puts on them; as opposed to the everloving family with two adoring children who always play nice and a dog that bounds in happiness before their every movement. Right here, Lindqvist twists what has become almost cliche in horror novels (the completely good ... and I understand, being a fan of horror, why the completely good is important) and then creates a supernatural event that will end up being the catalyst for so much. Simply, the child, a little brat named Maja, disappears "into thin air" (which is only barely appropriate) and the parents are left alone, worried, and shattered.<br /><br />Like Peter Straub's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19581.Ghost_Story" title="Ghost Story by Peter Straub" rel="nofollow noopener">Ghost Story</a>, this beginning works only to introduce the reader to the town. This town takes most of a small island and has a storied past. The population focuses on fishing for most of its income, and recently on tourism. It looks at the tourism business with a "one hand out, one hand clutching a knife" mentality, but for the most part lives along with the summer tourists (this recalls Shirley Jackson's "The Summer People", but from the reverse side). The story then blends past and present in a wonderful mixture. We are always one foot in the past and one foot in the present. Even without the dates (only there during the first 100 pages ... just to help the reader at the start), we soon get a firm enough knowledge of the island's history to know when we are looking at the past and when we are looking at the present. So much of this book is set-up for the last 200 pages, but what a set-up it is.<br /><br />But then the question pops up ... "What is the real story here?" Is it the search for a lost child? Is it the healing of a community? Or, as I contend, is it how do you let go? And that's also where this acts as the closing of the trilogy begun with Let The Right One In.<br /><br />To go much further into this book would create numerous spoilers. And yes, the last 50 or so pages barely hold up to the wonder before them. Frankly, the opening few sections sets up a lyrical myth that, as we get closer to the end and the darkness rises to the forefront, would be too difficult to close. So while I was gripped during the first 400 pages (entranced, mesmerized, possessed at times ... the like only happened when I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24800.House_of_Leaves" title="House of Leaves by Mark Z. Danielewski" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Leaves</a> a couple years back), the last 100 pages slogged through ice and knee deep water. It was sad to see it end that way.<br /><br />And yet, I feel that if I return to this book, I will look at those last few pages with new eyes and read the whole thing in a different way. And maybe, looking at this book as the closing of a trilogy, it will take on brand new meanings as I return to Let The Right One In and Handling The Undead (both of those also about different stages of loss). <br /><br />But Harbor is one of the few horror books that I recommend to non-horror readers. It is one of the few books that I have blabbed about to numerous folks as I walk with the book in my hand. This may be the best written book I've read this year ... and possibly longer. You won't understand until you get lost in the prose yourself and find yourself trapped on an island with horrible ghosts and decent, flawed people trying to make the best with what they have and not lose their souls along the way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10917050750452632153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_270350235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270350235" />
    <a title="Marvin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2160536-marvin"><img alt="Marvin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485672728p2/2160536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270350235?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marvin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marvin" href="/user/show/2160536-marvin">Marvin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 1921656670" href="/book/show/9972544-harbour">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2160536-marvin?shelf=horror">horror</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270350235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7557882433299287754"><i>Harbour</i> is a very impressive novel but ultimately failed to hook up to my emotions. It starts out beautifully. A child disappears on the frozen harbor during the winter. The father returns to the island and the harbor after two years. He is divorced and driven to alcohol. It is not really clear why he returns but it soon turns into not only a search for his child but also an investigation into the small community that lives on the island. The author contructs his tale by moving from present to p</span>
  <span id="freeText7557882433299287754" style="display:none"><i>Harbour</i> is a very impressive novel but ultimately failed to hook up to my emotions. It starts out beautifully. A child disappears on the frozen harbor during the winter. The father returns to the island and the harbor after two years. He is divorced and driven to alcohol. It is not really clear why he returns but it soon turns into not only a search for his child but also an investigation into the small community that lives on the island. The author contructs his tale by moving from present to past and the stories of the past takes on the feel of legends and folk stories. It is the back stories of this novel that hold the most interest. The book build up tension yet there is too much filler that takes us away from the father and his two friends to hold our attachment to the characters. Lindqvist continues to develop into a sort of Swedish Stephen King and he is almost there. <i>Harbour</i> is a a nice steppingstone to the probable future Lindqvist novel waiting to knock me over. Three and a half stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7557882433299287754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_546960511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/546960511" />
    <a title="Neil McCrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2141174-neil-mccrea"><img alt="Neil McCrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442523213p2/2141174.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/546960511?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil McCrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil McCrea" href="/user/show/2141174-neil-mccrea">Neil McCrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2141174-neil-mccrea?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2141174-neil-mccrea?shelf=ghost-stories">ghost-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2141174-neil-mccrea?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2141174-neil-mccrea?shelf=scandinavian">scandinavian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer546960511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2360515361679372907">Two things I often hear repeated about Lindqvist are that he's "Sweden's Stephen King" and that although his novels may make for excellent reading they're not <i>scary</i>. Regarding the first claim, I always felt that this was a combination of reviewer laziness and marketing wishful thinking . . . until Harbor. Harbor is very, very much in the style of King. A small town with secrets, a sizable supporting cast from every social strata, a seamless integration of pop culture references, and a strong sen</span>
  <span id="freeText2360515361679372907" style="display:none">Two things I often hear repeated about Lindqvist are that he's "Sweden's Stephen King" and that although his novels may make for excellent reading they're not <i>scary</i>. Regarding the first claim, I always felt that this was a combination of reviewer laziness and marketing wishful thinking . . . until Harbor. Harbor is very, very much in the style of King. A small town with secrets, a sizable supporting cast from every social strata, a seamless integration of pop culture references, and a strong sense of place and local colloquialisms, all of these attributes that I associate strongly with King are present here. Better yet, Lindqvist pulls it off.<br /><br />Everyone's mileage is going to vary in regards to fear factor, but Lindqvist is often more concerned with the horror of social breakdowns and fear of the unknown than with the adrenalized horrors of a slasher movie. I found myself more troubled by the largely harmless zombies of Handling the Undead precisely because figuring out what to do with mindless loved ones trying to reenact their old lives is more difficult than making the decision to blow the head off a shambling meat bag that's trying to eat me. The horror in Harbor is similar. Concern over how such sensible people could abide with a secret that puts all of their loved ones at risk is a greater source of worry in the novel than the question of whether an ominous force is going to "get" one character or another.<br /><br />The Harbor contains a masterful, ever growing sense of dread, cleverly delineated characters, and it mines a vein of horror that most authors never even attempt . . . soooooo . . . why the two stars? <br /><br />The ending.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'd call it a deus ex machina ending, except it's more problematic than that. The god in question (*cough* spiritus *cough*) doesn't pop up out of nowhere at the end of the story and save the day. It just sits prominently on the stage, seldom interacting with more than one character, never explained, and when it suddenly becomes instrumental to the climax of the novel it also becomes painfully clear that it has no narrative purpose other than to end things. It might as well have been a magic wand or the hand of god for all the difference it would have made. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="2360515361679372907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228073967?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mieneke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mieneke" href="/user/show/2485666-mieneke">Mieneke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2485666-mieneke?shelf=horror">horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228073967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2617437708536284518"><i>Harbor</i> was an intriguing novel. When I started it, I was a little apprehensive, as I was afraid I would be too scared – remember, I'm a wimp when it comes to reading horror – but while thrilling and frightening, it didn't give me nightmares. Instead its horror started with a creeping feeling of unease, of something off and, slowly, the true threat only becomes fully clear towards the end. I found myself eager to return to its pages each night and read until I had to turn off the light due to my </span>
  <span id="freeText2617437708536284518" style="display:none"><i>Harbor</i> was an intriguing novel. When I started it, I was a little apprehensive, as I was afraid I would be too scared – remember, I'm a wimp when it comes to reading horror – but while thrilling and frightening, it didn't give me nightmares. Instead its horror started with a creeping feeling of unease, of something off and, slowly, the true threat only becomes fully clear towards the end. I found myself eager to return to its pages each night and read until I had to turn off the light due to my eyes falling closed.<br /><br />One of my favourite elements of this novel were the narrative structure and Lindqvist's prose. The book is set up in a double narration with switching points of view between Anders and his grandfather Simon, with interspersed breaking of the fourth wall by an unknown narrator and short pieces from the point of view of other Domarö inhabitants. I love these kinds of twined narratives, as they provide not just a way for the author to give us more information about what's going – as the saying goes: two heads always know more than one – but they also provide opportunities for miscommunication or non-communication between characters, where the reader knows more than the protagonists. Coincidentally, it can also lead to a frustrated outcry of "Why don't they just talk to each other?", but Lindqvist never falls in that trap. Yes, there is non-communication, but he allows Simon to decisively put an end to that. Lindqvist's prose, through the translation of Marlaine Delargy, is clean and clear; no purple prose here, though his descriptions of the stark and isolated landscapes and the small island community are lovely, if at times chilling.<br /><br />I loved the character of Anders and I found the way Lindqvist describes his dealing with the loss of his daughter fascinating. The idea of losing one of my children – I'm already counting B2 as such, even if she isn't born yet – or my husband is my biggest nightmare and I thought Lindqvist dealt with both the madness of grief and the reshaping of memories beautifully. Anyone can picture what grief can drive someone too, whether drinking, like Anders, drugs, depression or self-harm. But I found Anders' reshaping his memories of Maja far more poignant, especially his inability to realise that he's done so until he's confronted about it by his grandparents. I think it's also something a lot of people don't realise—both that this is a natural reaction and that they've probably done the same with some of their own memories. All of this combined makes it hard to figure out whether what Anders thinks he's experiencing is true or whether they are delusions he's suffering due to too much alcohol consumption or grief.<br /><br />The other main narrator is Anders' sort of grandfather. He's been together with Anders' grandmother Anna-Greta for fifty years, though they never got married and is as much a grandfather as Anders has ever known. Despite having lived on Domarö for over half a century and being partnered with the unofficial leader of the island, Simon is still an outsider in many ways, as he finds out when he discovers the island's secret. But Simon is also more than just an old, retired stage magician, he has real magic, though what kind and how he came by it, is something best left for the reader to discover themselves. I really liked Simon, he is kind, strong and tenacious and I loved his relationship with Anna-Greta.<br /><br />Domarö and the sea are characters in and of themselves and are maybe the most frightening things in the book. Water can be the most destructive force on earth. It is everywhere and can penetrate everywhere. Water is patient and we humans cannot live without it. The Dutch have learnt to live with the fear of the encroaching water, to literally dam it out and in some ways to harness its amazing power, but we also know that water cannot be tamed and must always be respected. The inhabitants of Domarö respect and fear the sea in the same way, but in their need to placate the sea, they takes desperate and gruesome measures.<br /><br /><i>Harbor</i> is a stunning story, which made for compelling reading. If you are looking for an intelligent, spooky and mostly non-gory horror tale, this third offering by Lindqvist is just the ticket. I know this first taste of his writing has left me curious for more. I have already read <a href="http://scotspec.blogspot.com/2011/10/book-review-little-star-by-john-ajvide.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Niall's review</a> of Lindqvist's latest book <i>Little Star</i> and that sounds as good or even better as <i>Harbor</i> and I look forward to checking that out in the future.<br /><br />This book was sent to me for review by the <a href="http://us.macmillan.com/thomasdunne.aspx" rel="nofollow noopener">publisher</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2617437708536284518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17359312355021490336" style="display:none">Just a little off-topic here, isn't "harbor" spelled with a 'U'? "Harbour"? Or is "harbour" the Canadian and British variation of the word? There's a secret to the sea and the lighthouse where the incident occurred, and the book lets readers experience the suspense and solving as if it were real.</span>

  <span id="freeText11416868553914083661" style="display:none">This novel isn’t really a horror novel, to me. It was rather tense a couple times, but I wouldn’t classify it as horror. <div id="review_429388001" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/429388001" />
    <a title="Nate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62704-nate"><img alt="Nate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416938036p2/62704.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62704-nate?shelf=bookgrouppick">bookgrouppick</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62704-nate?shelf=2012">2012</a>,

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18338341328353386473">Bahf.<br/><br/>Quick summary: Man investigates his daughter's abduction from a small Swedish town with one huge disappointing secret.<br/><br/>I'm not much for horror novels, but even I thought this book wasn't scary. The plot floated on the surface of the water. It was as interesting as watching someone fish for hours.<br/><br/>SPOILERS AHOY AHOY <br/><br/>If you like books where the main character mopes a lot (Catcher In the Rye, Snow, anything by Jonathan Tropper) then pick this book up right away! The main character calls his ex-w</span>
  <span id="freeText18338341328353386473" style="display:none">Bahf.<br /><br />Quick summary: Man investigates his daughter's abduction from a small Swedish town with one huge disappointing secret.<br /><br />I'm not much for horror novels, but even I thought this book wasn't scary. The plot floated on the surface of the water. It was as interesting as watching someone fish for hours.<br /><br />SPOILERS AHOY AHOY <br /><br />If you like books where the main character mopes a lot (Catcher In the Rye, Snow, anything by Jonathan Tropper) then pick this book up right away! The main character calls his ex-wife often. He hangs out at his grandparents house wanting to talk about the past. He's haunted by two kids he knew when he was a teenager. He wallows in self-pity for most of the book. Which is understandable, having had his only daughter taken from him. It's just that you have to read 400 pages before he gets to doing anything about it.<br /><br />If you like books that have glimmers of good ideas that never pan out (The Magicians, The Submission, KMN Mrs. Dalloway), ooo-wee do I have a book for you! The Elin character was fascinating and should have been her own novel! But she gets killed right after we figure out why she's uglifying herself. That was a let down. The chapter where the main character realizes his daughter was a brat and that the pattern of brats being taken away by The Sea could have led somewhere meaningful. The other "brats" that were taken were barely mentioned and mostly were in there to support their brattiness. The magician background of the grandfather could have factored more into the plot and not in any ultra-powerful bug kind of way. The scene of the escape and the first reader inclination that the sea was inherently evil was genuinely. The idea of a blood hungry force of nature is compelling, especially in this day and age of superstorms, hurricanes, and droughts. <br /><br />The presence of Spiritus bothered me. It seemed way too easy for the author to give a human dominion over the nefarious character. It came out of nowhere and seemed only to be manipulated when the author wrote his way into a corner, plot-wise. The only way I would forgive its role in this plot is if Spiritus is some kind of well-known Scandinavian folk tale. Also, the fact that it was named the Latin word for air and breathe seems contrived. <br /><br />To me this book read as an underdeveloped cautionary tale of environmental changes. And that's where I'll leave it.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7618874652538653677">With 89 pages to go, I had to give it up. "Harbor" drifts around like an untied boat. I would guess the editors assumed Lindqvist was infallible from his previous successes so they checked a little grammar and approved the whole book.<br/><br/>The protagonist is a sad and pathetic drunk. These problems should have been at the center of the story's c</span>
  <span id="freeText7618874652538653677" style="display:none">With 89 pages to go, I had to give it up. "Harbor" drifts around like an untied boat. I would guess the editors assumed Lindqvist was infallible from his previous successes so they checked a little grammar and approved the whole book.<br /><br />The protagonist is a sad and pathetic drunk. His grandmother and her boyfriend were more interesting, but mysteriously they seemed unconcerned when the protagonist told them some of his serious problems. These problems should have been at the center of the story's conflict, but instead they felt like everyday episodes. "Oh yeah, such and such evil entities returned last night. Did you catch the game?"<br /><br />The book was too long and too unrewarding. It was not scary. By the end I did not give a crap what happened to the characters, so I read the last page. Really a disappointment. Reviewers calling it a "masterpiece" was absurd.</span>

<div id="review_205411515" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205411515" />
    <a title="E.  Nygma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5966687-e-nygma"><img alt="E.  Nygma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599770106p2/5966687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205411515?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="E.  Nygma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="E.  Nygma" href="/user/show/5966687-e-nygma">E.  Nygma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205411515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4854195609277454336">A real thriller. I disagree with the tag of "horror" genre, I think it will turn some people off from reading this book. Lindqvist has a way of taking a story and drawing you into it immediately. You can smell the smells, feel the textures, hear the sounds, you know the people he writes about as if you've known them forever.<br/><br/>Harbor is about several different people whose lives are intertwined on a small archipelago outside of Stockholm. A little girl vanishes right in front of her parents eyes, a</span>
  <span id="freeText4854195609277454336" style="display:none">A real thriller. I disagree with the tag of "horror" genre, I think it will turn some people off from reading this book. Lindqvist has a way of taking a story and drawing you into it immediately. You can smell the smells, feel the textures, hear the sounds, you know the people he writes about as if you've known them forever.<br /><br />Harbor is about several different people whose lives are intertwined on a small archipelago outside of Stockholm. A little girl vanishes right in front of her parents eyes, a couple whose love still burns as strong as the day they fell in love still live in separate houses next door to one another, a father keeps a tiny insect wormlike creature called a spiritus (spertus Norse mythology) in a box that requires a daily feeding or the consequences are dire and oddly, people just disappear every so often, without a trace and without rhyme or reason.<br /><br />Product Description<br /><br />It was a beautiful winter's day. Anders, his wife and their feisty six-year-old, Maja, set out across the ice of the Swedish archipelago to visit the lighthouse on Gavasten. There was no one around, so they let her go on ahead. And she disappeared, seemingly into thin air, and was never found. Two years later, Anders is a broken alcoholic, his life ruined. He returns to the archipelago, the home of his childhood and his family. But all he finds are Maja's toys and through the haze of memory, loss and alcohol, he realizes that someone - or something - is trying to communicate with him. Soon enough, his return sets in motion a series of horrifying events which exposes a mysterious and troubling relationship between the inhabitants of the remote island and the sea.<br /><br />From the Inside Flap<br /><br />They only stopped watching her for a couple of minutes. Which was all it took. <br /><br />On a clear winter's day, Anders took his wife and feisty six-year-old, Maja, for a walk from his home on the island across the frozen sea to the lighthouse at Gavasten. There was no one for miles around, so they stayed to admire the view while Maja struck out alone. <br />They never saw her again. <br /><br />Two years later and Anders' wife has left him, he's an unemployable alcoholic, so he returns to what's left of his family on the island. Moving back to the hut where he'd been staying with Maja that last time, he soon begins to feel a presence in the house. Could Maja be trying to communicate with him? Someone - or something - is leaving him messages and he can feel them getting stronger. <br /><br />Before long, it's not just a feeling and Anders starts seeing people who've been missing for years. Is it the drink or is he going mad? <br /><br />About the Author<br /><br />John Ajvide Lindqvist is a Swedish author, born 1968, grew up in Blackeberg, a suburb to Stockholm. He wanted to become something awful and fantastic. First he became a conjurer and came in second in the Nordic card trick championship, then he was a stand-up comedian for twelve years. John has written TV series as well as stage plays and TV drama. Two of his other novels, Let the Right One In and Handling the Undead have been translated into English and published by Quercus.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4854195609277454336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3421665401" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7898318613965163513"><i>Harbor</i> by John Ajvide Lindqvist is an intriguing horror mystery that will pull you in right from the opening. I wouldn't quite call it flat out scary, more unsettling and atmospheric than anything for me. Honestly, I'm not sure if any novel from this author will ever top my love of <i>Let the Right One In</i> as it set the bar so incredibly high. Oddly enough, I had the movie <i>The Lighthouse</i> (2019) in the back of my mind while reading this as I had watched the movie earlier this month. So, yeah, it was </span>
  <span id="freeText7898318613965163513" style="display:none"><i>Harbor</i> by John Ajvide Lindqvist is an intriguing horror mystery that will pull you in right from the opening. I wouldn't quite call it flat out scary, more unsettling and atmospheric than anything for me. Honestly, I'm not sure if any novel from this author will ever top my love of <i>Let the Right One In</i> as it set the bar so incredibly high. Oddly enough, I had the movie <i>The Lighthouse</i> (2019) in the back of my mind while reading this as I had watched the movie earlier this month. So, yeah, it was a bit of a strange reading experience.</span>

<div id="review_202195027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/202195027" />
    <a title="Rich Stoehr" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3710431-rich-stoehr"><img alt="Rich Stoehr" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547598466p2/3710431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/202195027?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rich Stoehr" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rich Stoehr" href="/user/show/3710431-rich-stoehr">Rich Stoehr</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3710431-rich-stoehr?shelf=amazon-vine">amazon-vine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer202195027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15689045006026470851">John Ajvide Lindqvist is an author who always seems to have a new trick up his sleeve, and <i>Harbor</i> is his best trick yet.<br/><br/>He pumped fresh blood into the vampire story with <i>Let the Right One In</i>, he gave new life to the zombie in <i>Handling the Undead</i>. With <i>Harbor</i>, he seemingly does the impossible, blending the characters and natural human conflicts of a good Stephen King novel with the sprawling menace of the stories of H.P. Lovecraft.<br/><br/><i>Harbor</i> is the story of a distant fishing community, almost ruined </span>
  <span id="freeText15689045006026470851" style="display:none">John Ajvide Lindqvist is an author who always seems to have a new trick up his sleeve, and <i>Harbor</i> is his best trick yet.<br /><br />He pumped fresh blood into the vampire story with <i>Let the Right One In</i>, he gave new life to the zombie in <i>Handling the Undead</i>. With <i>Harbor</i>, he seemingly does the impossible, blending the characters and natural human conflicts of a good Stephen King novel with the sprawling menace of the stories of H.P. Lovecraft.<br /><br /><i>Harbor</i> is the story of a distant fishing community, almost ruined by tourism and a brief popularity on travelogues, but still holding secrets only known to a select few. Disappearances, strange magic, visitations, and possession are only some of the strange events in store. While the full story stretches back generations, it begins for us with the disappearance of a young girl on the ice.<br /><br />This is the real trick Lindqvist pulls off in <i>Harbor</i>, taking an epic story and making it personal. Through the character of Anders we see the effect of the loss of his daughter, Maja, which tears apart both his marriage and his sanity. Through the characters of Simon and Anna-Greta we see the toll of secrets long-held, and the strain of a lifetime relationship. Through these very human and very vulnerable people the story is revealed...and we see how it will change them forever.<br /><br />There are unforgettable moments of fear in <i>Harbor</i>, from the ghosts who incessantly quote songs from The Smiths to a message scratched into a tabletop: "Carry me." There are moments of unimaginable scale and creeping dread, and moments of sweetness and intimacy.<br /><br />And there are many, many surprises.<br /><br />In <i>Harbor</i>, Lindqvist shows a magician's skill, making a seemingly impossible illusion look effortless - the grand vision of horror seen from very human eyes. It's a good trick, and he had me believing it all the way through to the last page.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15689045006026470851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14586796762810704167">This is a popular horror novel from Sweden. The story is compelling and well constructed. I am not a fan of this genre but this is a better example. Domaro is an island in a Swedish archipelago with a secret. People disappear and residents don't talk about these disappearances. Ander's small daughter becomes one of the disappeared and he leaves the island. Two years later he returns determine to get to the bottom of the mystery of her disappearance. Early on there is a sense of foreboding and te</span>
  <span id="freeText14586796762810704167" style="display:none">This is a popular horror novel from Sweden. The story is compelling and well constructed. I am not a fan of this genre but this is a better example. Domaro is an island in a Swedish archipelago with a secret. People disappear and residents don't talk about these disappearances. Ander's small daughter becomes one of the disappeared and he leaves the island. Two years later he returns determine to get to the bottom of the mystery of her disappearance. Early on there is a sense of foreboding and tension that is maintained throughout. For me the main drawback of this book is that it is 500 pages long.</span>

<div id="review_213316881" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/213316881" />

<div id="review_3472951025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3472951025" />

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 1921656670" href="/book/show/9972544-harbour">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18876665-sue-gerhardt-griffiths?shelf=2020-books">2020-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18876665-sue-gerhardt-griffiths?shelf=2020-intl-male-author-challenge">2020-intl-male-author-challenge</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3472951025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12728417558788630786">John Ajvide Lindqvist is known as a Swedish writer of horror novels, before becoming a published writer he was a magician and stand-up comedian. So, naturally my thinking was that his novel would incorporate fun and funny elements but that’s not to be, you won’t find magical fun or humour in this novel, although the blurb does state ‘a cocktail of suspense and bizarre humour,’ haha, I can agree with that, bizarre alright. <br/><br/>I rarely read horror but as this was my international male author challeng</span>
  <span id="freeText12728417558788630786" style="display:none">John Ajvide Lindqvist is known as a Swedish writer of horror novels, before becoming a published writer he was a magician and stand-up comedian. So, naturally my thinking was that his novel would incorporate fun and funny elements but that’s not to be, you won’t find magical fun or humour in this novel, although the blurb does state ‘a cocktail of suspense and bizarre humour,’ haha, I can agree with that, bizarre alright. <br /><br />I rarely read horror but as this was my international male author challenge book I wanted to read an author from a country other than England and America and this was the only book sitting on my bookshelves (sad, I know). <br /><br />If I dare to read a horror book I honestly want to be scared silly, I want a story that sends a chill across my skin and, makes my spine tingle, but there was no tingle, no chill, I was only mildly creeped out, nothing terrifying in the slightest which was a bit of a bummer.<br />Still, the claustrophobic remote island in the Swedish archipelago, the eerie atmosphere, the ominous sea, and the freakish wormwood thingy will keep the reader slightly jittery and transfixed until the final page is turned. <br /><br />A good thrillery story with supernatural elements. Creepy enough but won’t give you nightmares.<br /><br />*Book #8 of the 2020 International male author challenge</span>

<div id="review_202207874" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/202207874" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6022914-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421168922p2/6022914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/202207874?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/6022914-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781849165136" href="/book/show/9566003-harbour">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6022914-james?shelf=translated">translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6022914-james?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer202207874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4294452680532888044">It's a very different novel than <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/943402.Let_the_Right_One_In' title='Let the Right One In by John Ajvide Lindqvist' rel='nofollow noopener'>Let the Right One In</a>
</i>. Not just because it's a different subject and pace, it almost feels like it was written by a different author. Of course it is the same author, but it is a new translator. I had assumed that a translator just took the original text and translated it. Word x becomes y etc. Maybe move them about a bit to correct the grammar, but that was it. Turns out I may have underestimated that role pretty seriously unless Lindqvist is changing his sty</span>
  <span id="freeText4294452680532888044" style="display:none">It's a very different novel than <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/943402.Let_the_Right_One_In" title="Let the Right One In by John Ajvide Lindqvist" rel="nofollow noopener">Let the Right One In</a>
</i>. Not just because it's a different subject and pace, it almost feels like it was written by a different author. Of course it is the same author, but it is a new translator. I had assumed that a translator just took the original text and translated it. Word x becomes y etc. Maybe move them about a bit to correct the grammar, but that was it. Turns out I may have underestimated that role pretty seriously unless Lindqvist is changing his style from novel to novel. While my review of <i>Let the Right One In</i> suggested that I thought the characters came across as a bit clinical, this one is much more character driven. This novel is slower and that seems to give Lindqvist/Delargy more scope to develop the world that Lindqvist has created. Most of the story is explained through flashbacks and exposition provided through one character telling a story from their own past. Lindqvist seems to accept that this can sometimes be an unsatisfactory method of exposition, and even apologises at the start, yet it never feels forced or overly deliberate.<br /><br />The story itself is about the island of Domarö, a fictional island in a fictional archipelago off the coast of Sweden, and the pact that exists between its residents and the sea. The central character is Anders, an alcoholic, who is drawn back to the island where his young daughter, Maya, disappeared a couple of years before. Slowly, with his grandmother's partner Simon, he uncovers the history of the island and the individual relationships that many of it's residents have with the island and the sea around it. Eventually, Anders hopes, allowing him to find out what happened to his daughter. Although it's a supernatural story, it doesn't feel as dark or as 'gothic' as <i>Let the Right One In</i>, instead the supernatural powers seem more natural, almost incidental.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4294452680532888044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1288268823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1288268823" />
    <a title="Ian Laird" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28547777-ian-laird"><img alt="Ian Laird" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395488526p2/28547777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1288268823?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian Laird" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian Laird" href="/user/show/28547777-ian-laird">Ian Laird</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 1921656670" href="/book/show/9972544-harbour">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28547777-ian-laird?shelf=expected-more">expected-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28547777-ian-laird?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28547777-ian-laird?shelf=nordic">nordic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288268823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3736420052926423682">This otherwise quite interesting story came unstuck when one character gets a slug which he puts in a match box. <br/><br/>This is soon after we learn that Anders has lost his six year old daughter, Maja, vanished in the snow. <br/><br/>Here I need to introduce the spoiler early, just in case anyone wants to read John Ajvide Lindqvists’s <b>Harbour</b>. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ It’s a magic slug, and to be fairer than I have been so far, Lindqvist describes it as a larva or insect, so slug is my word. Anyway- slug in a matchbox. <br/><br/>T</span></span>
  <span id="freeText3736420052926423682" style="display:none">This otherwise quite interesting story came unstuck when one character gets a slug which he puts in a match box. <br /><br />This is soon after we learn that Anders has lost his six year old daughter, Maja, vanished in the snow. <br /><br />Here I need to introduce the spoiler early, just in case anyone wants to read John Ajvide Lindqvists’s <b>Harbour</b>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ It’s a magic slug, and to be fairer than I have been so far, Lindqvist describes it as a larva or insect, so slug is my word. Anyway- slug in a matchbox. <br /><br />The magic slug gives the holder or should I say close partner (the human holder) powers over water. And I’ve just realised that the fact that our human in this partnership, Simon, is, or once was, a magician is actually significant, because in a real sense he is able to use magic powers with the boxed insect. <br /><br />Simon is a denizen of Domaro, a remote island in the Swedish archipelago several hours from Stockholm. But he is a newbie, having been there a mere fifty years or so, in a lengthy relationship with Anna-Greta who is from a long line of Domarians who have a special relationship with the seas and its islands.<br /><br />It all gets very far fetched. I thought it was a mystery, and I was attracted to the book because it said loudly on the cover, from the author of <b>Let the Right One in</b>, the film adaptation of which I had enjoyed very much. Very promising.<br /><br />But no. It turns out this is a horror story, which is not what I had expected, but I persisted. Simon communes with the slug; the malevolent water exercises its vengeful spirit and a number of locals weird out under the strain, causing harm to themselves and others. Then it got fairly ridiculous, some Smiths fans made nuisances of themselves, after they were dead and Simon, sensibly no doubt, passed the slug onto Anders to help him find Maja. I lost interest when he started walking down a stairs and under the sea.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I’m sure this sort of scenario is not really what it’s like in Sweden. I hope.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3736420052926423682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_322251282" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322251282" />
    <a title="Brandon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9196784-brandon"><img alt="Brandon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335890896p2/9196784.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/322251282?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandon" href="/user/show/9196784-brandon">Brandon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer322251282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer303429748118220945">This book is set on a creepy little island in a Swedish archipelago. The folks who live there are interesting and well-rendered and a little weird. There is a big secret here, something awful, and the drunk, grieving protagonist has to uncover that secret. But of course, nobody wants him to.<br/><br/>I love so much about this novel. The characters are all fantastic, particularly the elderly magician, Simon. The setting is unique and the author takes time to fully explore it. He tells all manner of stories</span>
  <span id="freeText303429748118220945" style="display:none">This book is set on a creepy little island in a Swedish archipelago. The folks who live there are interesting and well-rendered and a little weird. There is a big secret here, something awful, and the drunk, grieving protagonist has to uncover that secret. But of course, nobody wants him to.<br /><br />I love so much about this novel. The characters are all fantastic, particularly the elderly magician, Simon. The setting is unique and the author takes time to fully explore it. He tells all manner of stories about that island, frequently jumping backward through time to grab little snippets of information that shed light on the present. This technique is a little rambling, but also quite satisfying.<br /><br />The only real problem I have is that the plot takes forever to get going. The characters don't do much. They are far more reactive than proactive. The book feels longer than it is because of that lack of plot. I probably spent a couple months reading this book because I seldom felt the need to pick it up. The plot is just not that compelling. But when I remembered to read the book, I greatly enjoyed my time with its fantastic cast of characters and eerie setting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="303429748118220945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17633819857443942533" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br />Anders, a man almost ruined following the disappearance of his young daughter, returns to the lighthouse where she wandered away across the ice, seemingly lost forever.<br />However, this is only the beginning of an epic, disjointed journey, not only his, but also the other residents of the island.<br />Weird, dream-like and with some really peculiar surrealism thrown in, I was often confused about where this tale was going, what was 'real' and what wasn't, but the mystery of the island held my attention, and I persisted in finding out what happened to Anders and Maya. Well, I made it to the end, but I'm still not entirely sure I understand how everything actually resolved itself, which is pretty annoying! (In my defense my brain was tired by this point) <br />Only recommended for Linqvist's most ardent fans, and people who enjoy long, meandering, bewildering epics. Personally I much preferred 'Let the Right One In'.<br />(I also don't understand why this is marketed as 'horror', it's more mystery with a tiny sprinkling of horror elements)</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132752689" />
    <a title="Leanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4483167-leanne"><img alt="Leanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340268814p2/4483167.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132752689?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leanne" href="/user/show/4483167-leanne">Leanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781849165112" href="/book/show/8447556-harbour">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132752689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15550626807900342637">I enjoyed reading Harbour, but I found the storyline to be weaker than his previous books - Let the Right One In and Handling the Undead. I think it lost its way towards the end and left too many unanswered questions.<br/><br/>It had its moments of suspense and a foreboding, yet it is not a horror story. It won't make you fear the sea, but it will make you see it differently. I found the book to be more of a character study, on what can happen to a person when they lose someone close to them - the self de</span>
  <span id="freeText15550626807900342637" style="display:none">I enjoyed reading Harbour, but I found the storyline to be weaker than his previous books - Let the Right One In and Handling the Undead. I think it lost its way towards the end and left too many unanswered questions.<br /><br />It had its moments of suspense and a foreboding, yet it is not a horror story. It won't make you fear the sea, but it will make you see it differently. I found the book to be more of a character study, on what can happen to a person when they lose someone close to them - the self destruction, guilt, fear, uncertainty and despair they struggle with. Yet it isn't all bad, we also see how hope and love is stronger than the evil in the world.<br /><br />Lindqvist is good at telling stories, he can make characters jump of the page and linger in your mind for days after finishing his books, and the settings are just as important as the stories. However, Harbour's plot feels rushed and not as well thought out. There's something missing and the ending just doesn't do the book justice.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15550626807900342637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3132660884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3132660884" />
    <a title="Phil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76396700-phil"><img alt="Phil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516033071p2/76396700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3132660884?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phil" href="/user/show/76396700-phil">Phil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76396700-phil?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76396700-phil?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3132660884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4169555255152201039">What a difficult book to describe or categorize! The story revolves around an island community in Sweden and while largely set in 2004 or so, there are large 'flashbacks' to decades and sometimes centuries earlier. Anders, our main protagonist, lives on the island with is wife and only child; one sunny winter day, they take a hike/ski to a lighthouse in the harbor for a picnic lunch. All is well until the child wanders off and never returns. A few years later, Anders returns to the island with a</span>
  <span id="freeText4169555255152201039" style="display:none">What a difficult book to describe or categorize! The story revolves around an island community in Sweden and while largely set in 2004 or so, there are large 'flashbacks' to decades and sometimes centuries earlier. Anders, our main protagonist, lives on the island with is wife and only child; one sunny winter day, they take a hike/ski to a lighthouse in the harbor for a picnic lunch. All is well until the child wanders off and never returns. A few years later, Anders returns to the island with a drinking problem after separating from his wife to the old cabin where they lived. His grandma and her partner Simon still live on the island. <br /><br />This seems relatively straight forward, but we are introduced along the way with magical insects and bits and pieces that let us know all is not right with the island. What at first seems like a simple tragedy of a lost child rapidly becomes an investigation to the power/monster that lives in the sea around the island and has defined the destiny of the island for generations. Is this a horror story? Maybe in a very slow burn kind of way, but more like magical realism run amok. <br /><br />Lindqvist tells an interesting story here, but this book could use some serious editing! </span>
  <a data-text-id="4169555255152201039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2981304289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5649274402562051969">Three and a half stars. Swedish literary horror novel about a dark force affecting a remote island community. The story develops slowly, with lots of character development and island history. (I found all of that interesting, so it didn't slow down the story that much for me.) Supernatural elements are slowly introduced as the plot progresses, leading to a more action-filled second half. <br/><br/>I think you have to be in the right mood for this book. If you're looking for a fast-paced horror story with </span>
  <span id="freeText5649274402562051969" style="display:none">Three and a half stars. Swedish literary horror novel about a dark force affecting a remote island community. The story develops slowly, with lots of character development and island history. (I found all of that interesting, so it didn't slow down the story that much for me.) Supernatural elements are slowly introduced as the plot progresses, leading to a more action-filled second half. <br /><br />I think you have to be in the right mood for this book. If you're looking for a fast-paced horror story with lots of gore and jump-scares, this isn't the book for you. I think the book is more on the weird, disturbing end of the horror spectrum. It's a little bit Harvest Home, a little bit Lovecraft, a little bit Ghost Story, but has its own original plot. Something a bit different.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5649274402562051969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_195788777" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195788777" />
    <a title="Paula" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3720054-paula"><img alt="Paula" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490570042p2/3720054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195788777?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula" href="/user/show/3720054-paula">Paula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781849165136" href="/book/show/9566003-harbour">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195788777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12305912179927359049">I am a fan of John Ajvide Lindqvist and 'Harbour' definitely met up to my expectations, you are engrossed from the first page, the story of Anders and his family and the history of Domaro is interesting and well written, it was not difficult to imagine the sights and sounds of Domaro and the ominous feeling of dread which clouds over the isolated town and the residents , who all share the same fear and have come to accept it and as the story progresses Anders begins to see what is wrong with Dom</span>
  <span id="freeText12305912179927359049" style="display:none">I am a fan of John Ajvide Lindqvist and 'Harbour' definitely met up to my expectations, you are engrossed from the first page, the story of Anders and his family and the history of Domaro is interesting and well written, it was not difficult to imagine the sights and sounds of Domaro and the ominous feeling of dread which clouds over the isolated town and the residents , who all share the same fear and have come to accept it and as the story progresses Anders begins to see what is wrong with Domaro and refuses to accept what has happened to Maja and faces the ghosts of Domaro and Gavasten in more ways than one. <br /><br />'Harbour' is a supernatural story with the added bonus of exploring the history of Domaro and the stories of the lives of the residents and what they have witnessed, the feelings of Anders are shown brilliantly, how much has character has changed because of the lost of his daughter and his marriage, his descent into deeper alcoholism is sad to read too. A story that will give you the creeps, so remember to lock your doors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12305912179927359049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_417173507" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/417173507" />
    <a title="Bandit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4528663-bandit"><img alt="Bandit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1289488158p2/4528663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/417173507?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bandit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bandit" href="/user/show/4528663-bandit">Bandit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer417173507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15297731642008190838">This novel was an epic. Definitely in volume, but also in scope, it covered (in great detail) the lives of generations of residents of a small island off the coast of Sweden. It was very easy at first to become engrossed with their lives, the author does some very good descriptive writing and he really spends a lot of time fleshing out his characters. The horror aspect in this book is less traditional...first it was his take on vampires, then on zombies, but in this story the antagonist is the s</span>
  <span id="freeText15297731642008190838" style="display:none">This novel was an epic. Definitely in volume, but also in scope, it covered (in great detail) the lives of generations of residents of a small island off the coast of Sweden. It was very easy at first to become engrossed with their lives, the author does some very good descriptive writing and he really spends a lot of time fleshing out his characters. The horror aspect in this book is less traditional...first it was his take on vampires, then on zombies, but in this story the antagonist is the sea itself surrounding the island, deep, dark and insiduous. I really enjoyed the writing and the characters, there were some genuinely terrifying situations and it was undeniably atmospheric, the main problem with this book was the pacing, it slowed and occasionally dragged making the book downright laborious to read. Recommended, but patience is required.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15297731642008190838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3nxgjVupfsHUCJGn+2aeoHHInFiGMR/WQqkm30TM5JwZ71JJpdFWZV3kRGK2VFS6p2EfWb57+Swcj2r6xE/Ocg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Dl5nsW69qj0Qq9/JbBqGExXZS7sZzX5+9l3ckCauwcrJzVV1kMWCmZlHCgwhKEwJw3DIuiGHmISoe5C1pi3rJA==')})
  }
